  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8e9ab716-d46b-4e6c-93ba-a3e6f9d4db17'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer4909589186240152343">"Sometimes it all comes over me," young Abbie said to her fiance, "that I can do big things. It's ahead of me...kind of like a light in the woods that shines and stays far away. And when I read verse or hear music...or...sing...it beckons me one, and my throat hurts with wanting to do something great."<br/><br/> Abbie Deal did do something great, even if it wasn't what she had dream</span>
  <span id="freeText4909589186240152343" style="display:none">"Sometimes it all comes over me," young Abbie said to her fiance, "that I can do big things. It's ahead of me...kind of like a light in the woods that shines and stays far away. And when I read verse or hear music...or...sing...it beckons me one, and my throat hurts with wanting to do something great."<br /><br /> Abbie Deal did do something great, even if it wasn't what she had dreamed of. And years later, when her children, raised in a rude sod hut, were prosperous men and women of a thriving state, she could say proudly, "I've seen everything...and I've hardly been away from this yard. I've seen the feeble beginnings of a raw state and the civilization that developed there, and I've been part of the beginning and part of the growth. But it's funny," she added, "I was always too busy filling up the youngsters and getting patches on the overalls to notice that I was part of the epic."<br /><br /> A strong an vigorous picture of pioneer life. The magnificent story of a young girl who went West as a bride -- and helped to build a nation.</span>

She didn't need to "appreciate" the last three quarters of <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I realize that I am a year out from your question. I do hope your daughter read this book. She didn't need to "appreciate" the last three quarters of the book. She only needed to connect to the people.<br />After 56 years, this is still one of the most influencing and impression making book I read as a 12 year old and believe me, as an only child on a farm, I read a LOT!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_312213468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/312213468" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2873459-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1258432776p2/2873459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/312213468?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/2873459-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer312213468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2798468928249277198">This book was beautifully written! I loved it! It was a simple, yet tender story of a pioneer woman-Abbie Deal. It is a book full of wisdom and so much insight. It is a book about mothering, and grandmothering and people and living. It made me reflect on myself, my own mother and grandma. It had so many wonderful quotes. Some of my favorite were:<br/><br/>"Because the road was steep and long,<br/>And through a dark and lonely land,<br/>God set upon my lips a song<br/>And put a lantern in my hand."<br/><br/>Here is another little </span>
  <span id="freeText2798468928249277198" style="display:none">This book was beautifully written! I loved it! It was a simple, yet tender story of a pioneer woman-Abbie Deal. It is a book full of wisdom and so much insight. It is a book about mothering, and grandmothering and people and living. It made me reflect on myself, my own mother and grandma. It had so many wonderful quotes. Some of my favorite were:<br /><br />"Because the road was steep and long,<br />And through a dark and lonely land,<br />God set upon my lips a song<br />And put a lantern in my hand."<br /><br />Here is another little gem she tells to her daughter,<br /><br />"You know, Grace, it's queer but I don't feel narrow. I feel broad. How can I explain it to you, so you would understand? I've seen everything...and I've hardly been away from this yard....<br />I've been part of the beginning and part of the growth. I've married...and borne children and looked into the face of death. Is childbirth narrow, Grace? Or marriage? Or death? When you've experienced all those things, Grace, the spirit has traveled although the body has been confined. I think travel is a rare privilege and I'm glad you can have it. But not every one who stays at home is narrow and not every one who travels is broad. I think if you can understand humanity...can sympathize with every creature...can put yourself into the personality of every one...you're not narrow...you're broad."<br /><br />And then here is one she tells her granddaughter:<br /><br />"You can't describe love, Kathie, and you can't define it. Only it goes with you all your life. I think that love is more like a light that you carry. At first childish happiness keeps it lighted and after that romance. Then motherhood lights it and then duty...and maybe after that sorrow. You wouldn't think that sorrow could be a light would you, dearie? But it can. And then after that, service lights it. Yes...I think that is what love is to a woman...a lantern in her hand." <br /><br />Ah….I just loved this book-simply lovely! There was so much to gain from this book-it made me want to be a better person. This is why it gets 5 stars. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2798468928249277198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3594036502" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3594036502" />
    <a title="Diane Barnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7262060-diane-barnes"><img alt="Diane Barnes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329773692p2/7262060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3594036502?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane Barnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane Barnes" href="/user/show/7262060-diane-barnes">Diane Barnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7262060-diane-barnes?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3594036502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7169604633198738290">This has been another of my beloved pioneer books. Recommended to me by Teresa, and egged on by Howard's review, I finally picked it up to read.<br/>An outwardly simple story of the settling and progress of Nebraska from 1867-1926, we see it all through the eyes of Abby Deal. Arriving in a covered wagon with her husband and baby boy, we are with her every step of the way. Droughts and fires and locusts, poor crops and bad years, the births of 5 more children, the struggle to raise them on next to not</span>
  <span id="freeText7169604633198738290" style="display:none">This has been another of my beloved pioneer books. Recommended to me by Teresa, and egged on by Howard's review, I finally picked it up to read.<br />An outwardly simple story of the settling and progress of Nebraska from 1867-1926, we see it all through the eyes of Abby Deal. Arriving in a covered wagon with her husband and baby boy, we are with her every step of the way. Droughts and fires and locusts, poor crops and bad years, the births of 5 more children, the struggle to raise them on next to nothing, and deaths of loved ones along the way.<br />Even with all the hard work and bad times, Abby had her dreams. First for herself, then for her children. Sacrifices are a natural part of parenthood, but even so, the dreams remain. There were several times in the reading of this that I was in tears, as sometimes fiction can make you realize your own reality. It gave me a greater understanding of what my own 91 year old mother had dealt with in her past, because even mothers were young and pretty once, before age does what it does.<br />Abby Deal portrays all women at some point in their lives, keeping on keeping on when everything seems lost, maintaining that fighting spirit against all that would hold her back, dealing with children and neighbors and history itself with compassion and charity. A truly enjoyable read. Thank you Teresa. Thank you Howard. Both of you were right about this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7169604633198738290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_14855818" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14855818" />
    <a title="Lucy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/307208-lucy"><img alt="Lucy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1233177432p2/307208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14855818?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy" href="/user/show/307208-lucy">Lucy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14855818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16880629063654682575">Originally published in 1928, Beth Streeter Aldrich uses this novel to create a fantastic female character, Abbie Deal. Abbie's story begins in 1854, when she is eight years old and at the start of a three week journey, traveling with her family by wagon from Illinois to Iowa. The fact that I grew up listening to pioneer stories from this era made her voyage very vivid in my mind. I could see the sacks of flour falling out of the wagon and floating in the river and the oxen slowly pulling all th</span>
  <span id="freeText16880629063654682575" style="display:none">Originally published in 1928, Beth Streeter Aldrich uses this novel to create a fantastic female character, Abbie Deal. Abbie's story begins in 1854, when she is eight years old and at the start of a three week journey, traveling with her family by wagon from Illinois to Iowa. The fact that I grew up listening to pioneer stories from this era made her voyage very vivid in my mind. I could see the sacks of flour falling out of the wagon and floating in the river and the oxen slowly pulling all the families' possessions along a bumpy buffalo trail. The story ends in 1926 with Abbie's death at the age of 80. The face of America changed dramatically between those years, and Abbie's life changed alongside it.<br /><br />Part pioneer story, part pride of Nebraska lesson, part farming tutorial, part commentary about marriage - Aldrich ultimately uses Abbie Deal to explain the choices and sacrifices that faced a 19th century woman, or more specifically, a mother.<br /><br />Perhaps Abbie Deal's selfless mothering is the source of my distress. I've always felt I've lacked in this arena and while I've tried really hard not to compare myself to my friends' and siblings' styles of mothering, I found myself forlorn with the realization that I was no Abbie Deal. Abbie was a natural mother. She postponed her dreams of becoming a singer and learning how to paint the prairie's sunset to follow her husband, Will, to Nebraska at the end of the Civil War.<br /><br />Originally, she postponed these dreams for the sake of her husband, who needed to carve his own way in life away from his father. Later she postponed them because there was no money or opportunity and every ounce of her energy went into building their home and farm and caring for her young children. Later yet, she postponed them because her children grew and had dreams of their own that required any extra time or money she had saved. Finally, she abandoned them altogether because her talents had left her. Her voice had faded from non-use and her fingers were gnarled and knobby from years of work. In the end, all she was left with was her good name and the pride she had in her children's accomplishments.<br /><br />Thus started the deep, stabbing pain in my chest. This kind of story, really...the universal story of motherhood, always leaves me feeling a little "damned if you do, damned if you don't". Abbie gave up everything of her own...her talents, her time, her figure (I can really relate to this), her life...for her children. The feminist in me resists....even feels slightly miserable that we women are expected and praised for being noble and altruistic, but void of personal achievement. The mother in me, however, wipes away a tear as I watch life from back stage instead of front and center, but wholly gets that my family is THE point. I get to clap and cheer and know that my efforts made this grand production possible.<br /><br />Throughout the book, Abbie does women a great service by allowing herself to wonder "what if". What if she had married that other boy who wanted her but who she didn't quite love, the one whose wife now wears all those fine clothes? What if she and Will hadn't moved to Nebraska and avoided suffering through drought and grasshoppers and blizzards? What if she had kept at her singing...developed the talent that everyone acknowledged she had? What if, what if, what if? What if I had? What then? Is the prize for the correct choice happiness?<br /><br />The fun in discussing this book would be hearing the strong arguments that defend both ends of the spectrum, and all the shades in between. Today, we lucky women choose the shade that fits us best. Do we like how we look?<br /><br />Abbie Deal chose motherhood but the story did not romanticize her choice. Abbie's story included every distracted husband, every sick child, every annoying friend and every moody child. And yet, in the end, Abbie sat as an old woman and felt satisfied that her five children were a fine product of a life's work.<br /><br />I recommend this book to every woman out there who enjoys tales of pioneer life or more importantly, empathizes with the difficult decisions made by women everywhere...always.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16880629063654682575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3571096279" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3571096279" />
    <a title="Howard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32041201-howard"><img alt="Howard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587918150p2/32041201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3571096279?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Howard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Howard" href="/user/show/32041201-howard">Howard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Howard by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/541416-teresa">Teresa</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32041201-howard?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32041201-howard?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32041201-howard?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32041201-howard?shelf=american-history">american-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32041201-howard?shelf=nebraska">nebraska</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32041201-howard?shelf=american-west">american-west</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32041201-howard?shelf=great-plains">great-plains</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32041201-howard?shelf=tall-woman">tall-woman</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3571096279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14712225665538646636"><blockquote>
  <b>Because the road was steep and long,<br/>And through a dark and lonely land,<br/>God set upon my lips a song<br/>And put a lantern in my hand.<br/> -- Joyce Kilmer</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>“A Lantern in Her Hand,” published in 1928, is good, old-fashioned storytelling at its best. Among other things for me, it was an island of tranquility that allowed me to temporarily escape today’s headlines and news stories, such as those about a once deliberative body, the U.S. Senate, in which one party had already made up its collective mind that </span>
  <span id="freeText14712225665538646636" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>Because the road was steep and long,<br />And through a dark and lonely land,<br />God set upon my lips a song<br />And put a lantern in my hand.<br /> -- Joyce Kilmer</b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br />“A Lantern in Her Hand,” published in 1928, is good, old-fashioned storytelling at its best. Among other things for me, it was an island of tranquility that allowed me to temporarily escape today’s headlines and news stories, such as those about a once deliberative body, the U.S. Senate, in which one party had already made up its collective mind that it was going to vote for the president’s Supreme Court nominee, no matter who that might be, while the other party had already made up its collective mind that it was going to vote against that nominee, no matter who that might be.<br /><br />So much for deliberation.<br /> <br />*****<br /><br />The novel opens in 1854, when its protagonist, Abbie Mackenzie, is eight-years old. She and her family, headed by her widowed mother, are migrating from Illinois to Iowa. After the Civil War, Abbie marries Will Deal, and they soon move to Nebraska, and it is there that most of the story takes place.<br /><br />Pioneer life was hard on men, but it was so much more difficult for women, and as a result it is a theme in many pioneer novels, including classics such as O.E. Rolvaag’s “Giants in the Earth,” an account of Norwegian immigrants in the Dakotas and Vilhelm Moberg’s Swedish settlers in his four books in his “The Emigrants” series, who eventually settle in Minnesota’s north woods. In those books the authors describe in graphic detail the hardships, loneliness, and despair experienced by pioneer women, and so did Beth Streeter Aldrich, though her book is a more optimistic account than the other two, especially “Giants in the Earth.”<br /><br />“A Lantern in Her Hand” was Aldrich’s best-selling book and most critics agreed that it was also her best book. One critic described her “as a romantic idealist who wrote of rural life in a positive sense, valuing its warmth and generosity of spirit, yet who was honest enough to show that it was not perfect.” <br /><br />Rolvaag’s and Moberg’s women did not want to leave their homes because of the heartbreaking knowledge that they would never again see the family members they left behind, and Aldrich’s Abbie Deal was no exception. “Will’s eyes, full of the light of hope and courage, looked to the west. But Abbie’s, tear-misted, clung to the east.” And when they finally reached their destination where they would make their home on the Nebraska prairie, Abbie looked around and saw that “save for the little clump of natural growth near the wagons, there was still not a tree in sight, not a shrub nor brush, a human being nor any living thing, -- nothing but the coarse prairie grass.”<br /><br />It could be a savage land, especially one in which to try to make a living as a farmer. The one constant factor in their favor was the rich, fertile, black soil; but at times that was not enough. Nature in that part of the world is not always an ally.<br /><br /><br /><blockquote>There are weeks when drifting snow and sullen sleet hold the Cedartown community in their bitter grasp. There are times when hot winds come out of the southwest and parch it with their feverish breath. There are monotonous droughts and periods of heavy rain; but between these onslaughts there are days so perfect, so filled with clover odors and rich, pungent smell of newly turned loam, so sumac-laden and apple-burdened, that to the prairie-born there are not others as lovely by mountain or lake or sea.</blockquote><br /><br /><br />And there were harsh times when Abbie could not overcome her despair. One of the very worst episodes occurred while she was expecting her fourth child when a plague of grasshoppers stripped the grain in the fields and destroyed the vegetables in the garden. It threw her into such a state of depression that she cried out loud, “God … you ought to help …. We can’t do it alone. You ought to help!”<br /><br />As I mentioned earlier, the book was a good escapist read for me, but I did not mean to infer that the story was a fantasy or a fairy tale. No, the life that these settlers lived was a hard one that they could not escape, but it also could be a rewarding one. And so the depression that descended on Abbie after the family was devastated by the loss of their crop and their garden did not last.<br /><br /><br /><b>“It seemed odd to Abbie to have a baby again after ten years. Sometimes she said she was afraid she had forgotten how to care for one. But when she grew strong, it all came back to her. The Abbie Deals do not forget.”</b> <br /><br /><br />And thus her normally optimistic nature returned, and she “went happily about her work … courage her lode-star and love her guide, -- a song upon her lips and a lantern in her hand.”<br /><br />*****<br /><br />Some readers of this review will remember our mutual friend Kirk, who left us all too soon. Kirk had a virtual shelf that he labeled “Strong Women.” I thought that was a great idea.<br /><br />I had read Wilma Dykeman’s classic novel, "The Tall Woman," a story about the struggles of a young pioneer woman living in the Appalachians in North Carolina, who had to first struggle to survive the Civil War, and then was forced to deal with that conflict’s uncertain aftermath. As a result, I decided to slightly alter Kirk’s idea and name my shelf “Tall Woman” as a way to honor both him and Wilma Dykeman.<br /><br />To date, I have thirty-two books, both fiction and nonfiction, on that shelf, though I may have overlooked a few when I went back looking for those that I had read prior to creating the shelf.<br /><br />I have written all of this to say that with “A Lantern in Her Hand,” we get two tall women for the price of one. The fictional Abbie Deal, of course, belongs on that shelf, but so does her creator.<br /><br /> In 1909, Bess Streeter Aldrich (1881-1954), her husband, and infant daughter moved from Iowa to Elmwood, Nebraska. It was there that Aldrich first began to write when she could find some time in between caring for her growing family and her housework. Her first book, a short story collection, was published in 1924.<br /><br />In 1925, her husband died as a result of a stroke, leaving Bess Aldrich with four children, the youngest four-years old and the oldest sixteen-years old. At the time of her husband’s death, she had published only two books, the aforementioned short story compilation and one novel. But from that point on, it was her writing that financially supported her family. She eventually published nearly 200 short stories and magazine articles, nine novels, one novella, and two short story collections.<br /><br /> She became a popular writer and one of the highest paid magazine writers of her times. And it was her writing that made it possible for her four children to obtain college degrees. <br /><br />One can’t help but believe that there was a lot of Bess Streeter Aldrich in Abbie Mackenzie Deal.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14712225665538646636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2816202849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15982101024134776863">I'm not a fan of pioneer books. That independant pioneer bravery is foreign to me, a lover of safety and comfort. Waxing romantic on endlessly waving fields just baffling to this devoted mountain girl.<br/><br/>But this is a book on motherhood, at heart, one of the most universal topics of all time. And I've never experienced a more poignant description of the endless pouring, pouring, pouring of self that motherhood has been for me.<br/><br/>A Lantern in Her Hand came to me at, perhaps, the best possible time. 5 y</span>
  <span id="freeText15982101024134776863" style="display:none">I'm not a fan of pioneer books. That independant pioneer bravery is foreign to me, a lover of safety and comfort. Waxing romantic on endlessly waving fields just baffling to this devoted mountain girl.<br /><br />But this is a book on motherhood, at heart, one of the most universal topics of all time. And I've never experienced a more poignant description of the endless pouring, pouring, pouring of self that motherhood has been for me.<br /><br />A Lantern in Her Hand came to me at, perhaps, the best possible time. 5 years ago it would have either enraged or depressed me. With a 1, 3, and 6 yr old, newly called to both homeschooling and fostering, I was in a place yelling to God, "When do I get to live MY life! Must I give everything to these children?" Aldrich emphatically says yes. <br /><br />Now my kids are older, and doubled in number. My friends all going back to school, or pursuing their dreams. And I'm still here. Still pouring. Accepting that there won't be an end. And it's beautiful. And worthy. And enough.<br /><br />"You know Grace, it's queer, but I don't feel narrow. I feel broad. How can I explain it to you, so you would understand? I've seen everything...and I've hardly been away from this yard."</span>
  <a data-text-id="15982101024134776863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_203231805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203231805" />
    <a title="wanderer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6155442-wanderer"><img alt="wanderer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386166906p2/6155442.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203231805?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="wanderer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="wanderer" href="/user/show/6155442-wanderer">wanderer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451161680" href="/book/show/4387768-a-lantern-in-her-hand">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6155442-wanderer?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6155442-wanderer?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6155442-wanderer?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203231805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11888599729111351523">Bess Streeter Aldrich does for pioneer Nebraska, what Margaret Mitchell does for the war-torn South: makes you want to live there, no matter how bad it was. <br/><br/>No matter how many times I read this book, I finish it with tears streaming down my face. It's not that the ending is so dreadfully sad, it's that the entire book makes me so emotional, and I keep fighting the sob session off until the end, when it all comes out in one gush. My husband caught me at it and said, "Boy, that must be one good bo</span>
  <span id="freeText11888599729111351523" style="display:none">Bess Streeter Aldrich does for pioneer Nebraska, what Margaret Mitchell does for the war-torn South: makes you want to live there, no matter how bad it was. <br /><br />No matter how many times I read this book, I finish it with tears streaming down my face. It's not that the ending is so dreadfully sad, it's that the entire book makes me so emotional, and I keep fighting the sob session off until the end, when it all comes out in one gush. My husband caught me at it and said, "Boy, that must be one good book." He knows me well, and he's right.<br /><br />This time through, I noticed some rather unpleasant writing quirks: over-use of repetition, weird pacing, and ellipses galore. Under some circumstances, this would turn me off a book entirely, but I forgive Aldrich all and quickly go on to her next book. <br /><br />She makes me feel what it meant to be a pioneer. She celebrates women. She somehow reaches across the years and miles and touches on issues I care about, expresses feelings I thought only I felt, and makes me feel and care and--like I said--cry my eyes ugly. <br /><br />Abbie Deal is a true literary heroine, in my eyes. She's my great grandma and my mother. She's me, and she's my nieces and greats, someday. She's a women, and she does "what women do." <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11888599729111351523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2916837004" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2916837004" />
    <a title="Cindy Marsch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5910164-cindy-marsch"><img alt="Cindy Marsch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533037123p2/5910164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2916837004?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy Marsch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy Marsch" href="/user/show/5910164-cindy-marsch">Cindy Marsch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5910164-cindy-marsch?shelf=5-star-reviews">5-star-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2916837004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer370397641915948875">This amazing little book is cathartic for any mother to read--cautionary for the young mother, bracing for the emptying-nest mother, and consoling for the older mother. It is a reminder that our joys and disappointments, our hopes and griefs, are not new to our generation nor individual to ourselves. <br/><br/>It's a bit of a shock to learn this volume was written in 1928, and as Aldrich describes the glorious abundance of the Nebraska crops of that time, it's sobering to think that she had no idea what w</span>
  <span id="freeText370397641915948875" style="display:none">This amazing little book is cathartic for any mother to read--cautionary for the young mother, bracing for the emptying-nest mother, and consoling for the older mother. It is a reminder that our joys and disappointments, our hopes and griefs, are not new to our generation nor individual to ourselves. <br /><br />It's a bit of a shock to learn this volume was written in 1928, and as Aldrich describes the glorious abundance of the Nebraska crops of that time, it's sobering to think that she had no idea what was about to come--with the Crash and the Dust Bowl. But she would have said that indeed Abbie Mackenzie Deal went out at the high mark and would have taken the privations to come in their turn, as she'd taken all her life. I expect her middle-aged, prosperous children would recall the poverty of their pioneer childhood and--as she would have wished--take the turn of fortune in stride. That's the work of a generation: to prepare the next generation for what is to come by building resilience into their character, by teaching them how to take joy in the color of the sky, by showing how it may all be done. As my own grandmother took me aside and confided in me some things she knew her daughter could not appreciate nor bear, as she was so close to them, Abbie Deal found confidantes among her granddaughters, and she died in satisfaction.<br /><br />It's sort of embarrassing reading this book, as its cover (mine is worse than the one displayed here--mine is a sixties ingenue in a "granny dress" with her sleek hair piled up in a ribbon) suggests a <br />"slight" work. Instead this novel is heavy for its size, dense and grounding.</span>
  <a data-text-id="370397641915948875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_858702867" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/858702867" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4228578-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354685047p2/4228578.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/858702867?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/4228578-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/21863588-a-lantern-in-her-hand">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer858702867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3200011794165327247">I really enjoyed this book. It feels like finding a hidden treasure when I discover a great book written long ago that I've never heard of. I struggled for a while with the style of the prose, but the story was gripping and I couldn't put it down. I was also impressed with the integrity of the protagonist and the value she placed on her role as a mother. The story is a tribute to mothers of every generation, I think, and the sacrifices they make for their children.<br/><br/>Note: I got my copy from interl</span>
  <span id="freeText3200011794165327247" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book. It feels like finding a hidden treasure when I discover a great book written long ago that I've never heard of. I struggled for a while with the style of the prose, but the story was gripping and I couldn't put it down. I was also impressed with the integrity of the protagonist and the value she placed on her role as a mother. The story is a tribute to mothers of every generation, I think, and the sacrifices they make for their children.<br /><br />Note: I got my copy from interlibrary loan at our state university and it is a first edition. The original owner (in 1929) pasted a newspaper clipping on the inside front cover. I thought it should be shared here. Unfortunately, the clipping doesn't show the name of the newspaper or when it was published. <br /><br />"A PIONEER MOTHER: In her new novel, "A Lantern in her Hand," published by Appleton, Bess Streeter Aldrich says she has told many of the stories of the pioneers and the early days on the prairies which she heard from her parents. In describing how she came to write this novel, Mrs. Aldrich says "My parents, having come into Iowa before their marriage, were always full of the experiences of those early days, and so I was steeped in an atmosphere of reminiscences of river floods, storms, drought, ox-team trails, log cabins and snow drifting onto beds. Once in later years after I had begun to write and my mother was a very old lady, I remarked to her how sorry I was that she endured such a hard life when she was young. She looked at me with an odd sort of an expression and said, 'Save your pity. We had the best time in the world.' Suddenly it seemed to me that I would like to catch a little of that spirit in a story sometime--that I wanted to write some day a pioneer mother who, although she endured all the hardships of those days, was sustained through it all by courage and love and a sense of humor. I think I would have written "A Lantern in Her Hand" if I had known a single copy would not be sold. It is my bit to honor the pioneer mother."</span>
  <a data-text-id="3200011794165327247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Nicole Miller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1082719-nicole-miller"><img alt="Nicole Miller" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46400151?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole Miller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole Miller" href="/user/show/1082719-nicole-miller">Nicole Miller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46400151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11847620480994025252">Maybe it's because this author is predictable and I only recently read another book by her, but I am finding that one of the reasons I don't enjoy Pioneer era historical fiction is because it's all very predictable. They all go like this...They head west, the woman doesn't really want to go, but she has no say, so she goes along anyway, promising to visit her family (she never does). They have a hard time getting west and someone dies. They finally make it west, the first winter is hard and some</span>
  <span id="freeText11847620480994025252" style="display:none">Maybe it's because this author is predictable and I only recently read another book by her, but I am finding that one of the reasons I don't enjoy Pioneer era historical fiction is because it's all very predictable. They all go like this...They head west, the woman doesn't really want to go, but she has no say, so she goes along anyway, promising to visit her family (she never does). They have a hard time getting west and someone dies. They finally make it west, the first winter is hard and someone dies. The first crop is unsuccessful, and someone dies the following winter...slowly the crops might get a little more successful, but more than likely someone will die just about every other year and usually it's a child. <br />I know it's true to life, but, it's just not a life story I want to read I guess. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11847620480994025252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_105251760" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105251760" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/612636-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504072309p2/612636.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105251760?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/612636-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Beth by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2345696-meagan">Meagan</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105251760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3792919175445184691">Ah, a beautiful, bittersweet book. It felt epic in places, sweeping over generations, and yet it contained small vignettes and tightly-wound themes that reminded me of a short story.<br/><br/>Some of the themes included:<br/><br/> * Choices. The choice discussed in the summary between marrying the doctor or the farmer reminded me of the famous Frost poem, about two roads diverging in a wood. That choice really did “make all the difference” to Abbie Deal — and to her posterity.<br/> * Loyalty and Friendship. Loved the fr</span>
  <span id="freeText3792919175445184691" style="display:none">Ah, a beautiful, bittersweet book. It felt epic in places, sweeping over generations, and yet it contained small vignettes and tightly-wound themes that reminded me of a short story.<br /><br />Some of the themes included:<br /><br /> * Choices. The choice discussed in the summary between marrying the doctor or the farmer reminded me of the famous Frost poem, about two roads diverging in a wood. That choice really did “make all the difference” to Abbie Deal — and to her posterity.<br /> * Loyalty and Friendship. Loved the friendship between Sarah and Abbie — and even moreso between Abbie and Christine. These women were true to each other, even in hard times.<br /> * Sacrifice. Oh, the sacrifices a parent makes for a child! I was lucky enough to have a mother that gave me many opportunities, ones that she herself never had while she was growing up. I couldn’t help but reflect on that as I read.<br /> * Time. The way the author describes the hands on the clock sweeping away the hours is hauntingly beautiful.<br /> * Age. I loved how the story came full circle, and the reader realizes that “Old Lady Deal” that we meet in the beginning had a full, rich life — full of memories. It made me think differently about my parents and grandparents.<br /><br />This was so much more than the typical pioneer story. The heroic Abbie Deal is one of my new favorite characters from literature; she was strong and yet unselfish, a strange balance of feminism that is so rare. And she really does personify the poem from which the title was based:<br /><br /> Because the road was steep and long,<br /> And through a dark and lonely land,<br /> God set upon my lips a song<br /> And put a lantern in my hand.<br /> –Joyce Kilmer</span>
  <a data-text-id="3792919175445184691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Vicki B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5675076-vicki-b"><img alt="Vicki B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325696160p2/5675076.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/213877556?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vicki B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vicki B" href="/user/show/5675076-vicki-b">Vicki B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780803259225" href="/book/show/3471099-a-lantern-in-her-hand">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5675076-vicki-b?shelf=most-moving-powerful">most-moving-powerful</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer213877556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13146811550331751589">I wonder...if I had read this book at a younger age, would it have moved me in the same profound way? I've raised my children, have grandchildren, worked hard (seemed hard to me, tho' almost laughable comparable to Abbie Deal...who's story more resembles my incredible mother-in-law's) done without, had dreams, given up on dreams. So many of the musings Bess Streeter Aldrich's character has throughout her life resemble my own--some of the later ones I hadn't even given words to!<br/><br/>What a marvelous, </span>
  <span id="freeText13146811550331751589" style="display:none">I wonder...if I had read this book at a younger age, would it have moved me in the same profound way? I've raised my children, have grandchildren, worked hard (seemed hard to me, tho' almost laughable comparable to Abbie Deal...who's story more resembles my incredible mother-in-law's) done without, had dreams, given up on dreams. So many of the musings Bess Streeter Aldrich's character has throughout her life resemble my own--some of the later ones I hadn't even given words to!<br /><br />What a marvelous, exhaustive, thorough reminding of what it took to settle &amp; develop our country this book is to us that have it so very easy. May we continue the telling &amp; never forget.<br /><br />One thought that stands out is the richness of Abbie's self-sacrificing life as compared to the more shallowness of the next generation who have the time &amp; means to seek out "time for themselves". She had her battles with bitterness from time to time, especially at the loss of some of her girlhood dreams, but in the end when her granddaughter Laura asks her happiest memory she says: <br /><br />"...I like to think of the table set for the whole family at supper time. The robins are singing in the cottonwoods and the late afternoon sun is shining across the floor. Will, your grandfather, is coming in to supper..and the children are all playing out in the yard. I can hear their voices and happy laughter." (p. 284)<br /><br />I feel much the same.<br /><br /> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13146811550331751589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11655862508960957979" style="display:none">Loved it! The novel, which describes the whole life of a pioneer woman named Abbie, was beautifully written and sprinkled with simple yet profound thoughts. I got so attached to Abbie and Will that the book made me all emotional. The writing style was like a mix between L.M. Montgomery and Janette Oke, with something unique added in.<br /><br />Sometimes a span of 5 years or so was mentioned by only a brief paragraph, which I didn't particularly like, but the author made up for it with detailed descriptions of the times that she did include. <br /><br />Glad I read this! 4.5 stars.</span>

<div id="review_60034897" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60034897" />
    <a title="Jodi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1052593-jodi"><img alt="Jodi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332344040p2/1052593.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/60034897?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jodi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jodi" href="/user/show/1052593-jodi">Jodi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1052593-jodi?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1052593-jodi?shelf=book-group">book-group</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60034897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7833825952628905275">I read this book for a book group and it is also the state of Nebraska book choice of the year--being a story about a pioneer family moving to and settling in Nebraska.<br/><br/>Since I, myself recently moved to Nebraska because of my husband's work, I did find myself sympathizing with Abbie at the beginning as she tried to convince her husband that there was nothing to go to Nebraska for and her lack of excitement about the move. I too, never thought I'd ever live in Nebraska, but like Abbie, a century l</span>
  <span id="freeText7833825952628905275" style="display:none">I read this book for a book group and it is also the state of Nebraska book choice of the year--being a story about a pioneer family moving to and settling in Nebraska.<br /><br />Since I, myself recently moved to Nebraska because of my husband's work, I did find myself sympathizing with Abbie at the beginning as she tried to convince her husband that there was nothing to go to Nebraska for and her lack of excitement about the move. I too, never thought I'd ever live in Nebraska, but like Abbie, a century later I'm thoroughly enjoying it.<br /><br />I've had trouble deciding what rating to give this book. I was disappointed at how much time the book covered, from Abbie's childhood clear until her old age and death. I thought it was a little much to cover in a 250 page book. I felt like I was reading a lot of brief descriptions summarizing what happened over a 5 or 10 year period without going too deep into a plot or taking time to let me fall in love with the characters. The second half of the book also had so many characters (with all of Abbie's children, grandchildren, and even great-grandchildren) I often got confused with the relationships and keeping track of who was who, but that might also be due to my level of sleepiness while reading. <br /><br />Other times throughout the book the "clock" so to say, would stop for a while and the author would actually take time to tell about a specific event in detail with dialogue between the characters. I seemed to like those scenes much more than the descriptions of the passage of time.<br /><br />I found it humorous how often the author described or mentioned Abbie's "tapered fingers". I didn't quite understand why the author liked using that description so much. I found myself chuckling each time it was mentioned over and over.<br /><br />Overall, not a bad book but not a great one either. I've read other pioneering stories that I have enjoyed much more. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7833825952628905275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1454407792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9830899279402199753">Wow. I only picked up this book because someone recommended A White Bird Flying by the same author and suggested I read this prequel first. I thought it would just be a simple read to get through before reading the next and was not prepared for the profound truths about which this book speaks.<br/><br/>These truths, choosing a spouse, raising your children, dying to self, were so clearly articulated through the fictional character of Abbie Deal. I was both amused and shocked at learning about life on the </span>
  <span id="freeText9830899279402199753" style="display:none">Wow. I only picked up this book because someone recommended A White Bird Flying by the same author and suggested I read this prequel first. I thought it would just be a simple read to get through before reading the next and was not prepared for the profound truths about which this book speaks.<br /><br />These truths, choosing a spouse, raising your children, dying to self, were so clearly articulated through the fictional character of Abbie Deal. I was both amused and shocked at learning about life on the Nebraska prairie in the late 1800's. But I was moved to tears by the lessons in this book. And through my tears I was smiling at the realization that motherhood is the same now as it was a hundred years ago. And the love between a husband can be the same if you are blessed with a spouse like Will Deal. <br /><br />This book made me appreciate what I have. It made me stop and linger while tucking my children into bed. It made me find the beauty and goodness in something as simple as setting the table for my family. It's a book that will likely stay with me forever.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1444437" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1444437" />
    <a title="Chelsea Cripps" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/98807-chelsea-cripps"><img alt="Chelsea Cripps" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1183163529p2/98807.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1444437?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Cripps" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Cripps" href="/user/show/98807-chelsea-cripps">Chelsea Cripps</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1444437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8354999440912873770">I read this one for my church book club. As soon as I heard the title, I recognized it as one of my mother's favorite ever books. I read it in high school, upon her insistance, and remembered only that it was "really cheesey." On a second read, it was less cheesey than I remembered (though still a little bit) and in fact, I found it an incredibly sad novel. It's the story of a young girl around the turn of the 20th century, who has all these big girlish dreams of becoming a beautiful singer, a p</span>
  <span id="freeText8354999440912873770" style="display:none">I read this one for my church book club. As soon as I heard the title, I recognized it as one of my mother's favorite ever books. I read it in high school, upon her insistance, and remembered only that it was "really cheesey." On a second read, it was less cheesey than I remembered (though still a little bit) and in fact, I found it an incredibly sad novel. It's the story of a young girl around the turn of the 20th century, who has all these big girlish dreams of becoming a beautiful singer, a painter, a writer--she just has this "feeling" that she is going to grow up to be something special. And she really does have a lovely voice and is encouraged to go to New York and study. She even gets a marriage proposal that would make it all possible, but she turns it down to marry her true love and follow him out west to settle Nebraska. As the book goes on, they have children, eek out a living establishing a farm and a state out west and each of her dreams gets put off and put off until eventually she is an old woman and realizes it is too late for any of her dreams. But, each of her dreams is carried out by one of her children--one becomes a painter, one a singer, one an explorer etc etc. I know this is supposed to be inspiring and heart warming, but I just find it so depressing. There are a couple of really beautiful and heart breaking scenes near the end where she watches her children go and and achieve their (her) dreams, and she has a little cry, born of pride, but also of sadness. Those are very bittersweet moments.<br />Overall, not the best writing in the world, but not as write-offable as I initially <br />categorized it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8354999440912873770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1068232378" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1068232378" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/582793-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457578611p2/582793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1068232378?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/582793-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1068232378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10352185521846811113">I just finished this book and can tell it's going to be one that I reflect on the rest of my life. It was beautifully written and scattered with many tidbits of wisdom. It was so enjoyable to see a whole lifetime lived in one book. <br/><br/>I found myself admiring and learning from the main character, Abbie Deal, through all her stages of motherhood and grand-motherhood. She was so good at loving her children despite their varying personalities, loving her husband for his unique strengths, and snapping o</span>
  <span id="freeText10352185521846811113" style="display:none">I just finished this book and can tell it's going to be one that I reflect on the rest of my life. It was beautifully written and scattered with many tidbits of wisdom. It was so enjoyable to see a whole lifetime lived in one book. <br /><br />I found myself admiring and learning from the main character, Abbie Deal, through all her stages of motherhood and grand-motherhood. She was so good at loving her children despite their varying personalities, loving her husband for his unique strengths, and snapping out of personal low points through gratitude and hard work. She was fiercely loyal to her friends and lived a simple yet rich life. It was interesting to see the contrast of how her family turned out vs. other families in the story based on the way she nurtured her children and the values she taught them. I also appreciated how she learned to bloom where she was planted. She chose to love the prairie and in turn, it became beautiful in her eyes. I especially enjoyed the author's take on death and her description of what it will be like. <br /><br />I think the strength I most admired in Abbie was her ability to hold her tongue when she heard her older children and grandchildren share differing opinions with her. In doing so, she maintained close relationships, gave herself room to change her opinions of them as they grew older, and never made them feel judged by her. That one strength left the door open for all of her posterity to want to return to her time and time again and feel nothing but love from her.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10352185521846811113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10162271337073851422">Wow, I have never been moved by a story as much as I was by this one. I think I cried over nearly every chapter in the second half of the book, and I sobbed my way through the last two! Being a native Nebraskan, having pioneers like Abbie Deal for ancestors, I knew this book would resonate with me. But I wasn’t prepared for how closely I would identify with Abbie’s dreams, hopes, and longings. I had no idea how much her story as a wife and mother would touch deep chords within my heart. Needless</span>
  <span id="freeText10162271337073851422" style="display:none">Wow, I have never been moved by a story as much as I was by this one. I think I cried over nearly every chapter in the second half of the book, and I sobbed my way through the last two! Being a native Nebraskan, having pioneers like Abbie Deal for ancestors, I knew this book would resonate with me. But I wasn’t prepared for how closely I would identify with Abbie’s dreams, hopes, and longings. I had no idea how much her story as a wife and mother would touch deep chords within my heart. Needless to say, I will be returning to this books again in future seasons of my life. If I never had a “heart book” before, I most certainly do now.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51364272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1964204037345988085">This was a very interesting book. It was more like I felt my way from cover to cover than read it. I don't even know if that makes sense but the way that the author painted the story - the images, the feelings, the experiences - was so amazing.<br/><br/>This book was first published in 1928 and is about the settling of Nebraska. But it reaches further back and forward than just another pioneer story. It is also about family and a mother's heart, dreams, friends and reality.<br/><br/>I would wholeheartedly recommend</span>
  <span id="freeText1964204037345988085" style="display:none">This was a very interesting book. It was more like I felt my way from cover to cover than read it. I don't even know if that makes sense but the way that the author painted the story - the images, the feelings, the experiences - was so amazing.<br /><br />This book was first published in 1928 and is about the settling of Nebraska. But it reaches further back and forward than just another pioneer story. It is also about family and a mother's heart, dreams, friends and reality.<br /><br />I would wholeheartedly recommend this book to anyone.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3371177951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9736947902839677438">This is a lovely work of fiction, based loosely on the author's mother, about the long and busy life of a woman who arrived in Nebraska as a pioneer and lived long enough to see people and machinery transform the bald prairie. <br/>I thought it would focus on the early days, but instead it follows Abbie Deal through marriage, children, and widowhood right up to her death. Throughout, her abiding passion is her love of nature and family. <br/>She expresses some beautiful philosophical thoughts about life. </span>
  <span id="freeText9736947902839677438" style="display:none">This is a lovely work of fiction, based loosely on the author's mother, about the long and busy life of a woman who arrived in Nebraska as a pioneer and lived long enough to see people and machinery transform the bald prairie. <br />I thought it would focus on the early days, but instead it follows Abbie Deal through marriage, children, and widowhood right up to her death. Throughout, her abiding passion is her love of nature and family. <br />She expresses some beautiful philosophical thoughts about life. This quote sums it up: “I think that love is more like a light that you carry. At first childish happiness keeps it lighted, and after that, romance. Then motherhood lights it and then duty . . . and maybe after that sorrow. You wouldn’t think that sorrow could be a light, would you, dearie? But it can. And then after that, service lights it. Yes. . . . I think that is what love is to a woman . . . a lantern in her hand.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="9736947902839677438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17777909362327519042">I'm sadly abandoning this one after reading 14 chapters. I really, really want to love this book because it has so much potential, but the author is holding me at a distance and won't let me hang out with Abbie Deal. Lots of telling and not enough showing. I'm told that Abbie and Sarah are best friends, but I've never seen them visit each other or talk to each other; I'm told that Abbie loves her children but I never hear her talk to them and I don't even know the color of their hair or anything</span>
  <span id="freeText17777909362327519042" style="display:none">I'm sadly abandoning this one after reading 14 chapters. I really, really want to love this book because it has so much potential, but the author is holding me at a distance and won't let me hang out with Abbie Deal. Lots of telling and not enough showing. I'm told that Abbie and Sarah are best friends, but I've never seen them visit each other or talk to each other; I'm told that Abbie loves her children but I never hear her talk to them and I don't even know the color of their hair or anything about their personalities; and the list goes on.<br /><br />I keep thinking that if I want to read Little House on the Prairie for Grownups (and I do), I should wrap myself up in a Willa Cather or William Maxwell masterpiece. Hmm...what a great idea...I'm off to read some William Maxwell. :)</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2070132542" />
    <a title="Ashley Jacobson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17846660-ashley-jacobson"><img alt="Ashley Jacobson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530340775p2/17846660.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Jacobson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Jacobson" href="/user/show/17846660-ashley-jacobson">Ashley Jacobson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780803259225" href="/book/show/3471099-a-lantern-in-her-hand">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17846660-ashley-jacobson?shelf=read-fiction">read-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17846660-ashley-jacobson?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2070132542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11339644015113600666">2020- This is my 3rd time through in a year. This book is such a beautiful ode to motherhood and the sacrifices a mother makes. While Abbie’s case is extreme and some argue that she gave up too much, she would never feel that way. Her family was worth every sacrifice. She worked to make sure her kids and grandkids had a better life than she did. And they did. But home was always a place to come back to. This is so much more than a pioneer book. It’s a work on motherhood and womanhood. It’s a rem</span>
  <span id="freeText11339644015113600666" style="display:none">2020- This is my 3rd time through in a year. This book is such a beautiful ode to motherhood and the sacrifices a mother makes. While Abbie’s case is extreme and some argue that she gave up too much, she would never feel that way. Her family was worth every sacrifice. She worked to make sure her kids and grandkids had a better life than she did. And they did. But home was always a place to come back to. This is so much more than a pioneer book. It’s a work on motherhood and womanhood. It’s a reminder that our memories will one day become our most valuable possessions. It’s just beautiful! <br /><br />2019- Perfection. I don’t know how to review this book. Others have impacted me about as much, but none were as satisfying as this. It spoke to me as a mother in a way no other book has (and probably more so since I just had baby #3). It was hard. I must say I wish someone would have warned me how many babies die in this book. That was hard to read after just having one of my own. But it was so worth it. Abbie is amazing and a character I will always carry with me. I will be revisiting this book regularly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11339644015113600666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/116302280?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary JL" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary JL" href="/user/show/1734736-mary-jl">Mary JL</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1734736-mary-jl?shelf=fiction-classics">fiction-classics</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116302280" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1370472956665731023">This is a beautiful, poetic moving story of Abby Deal, covering the time of the early pioneer settlements in the Midwest.<br/><br/>It is a timeless family story of a mother who sees the dreams she is unable to fulfill passed on to her children. Realistic--with both sad and funny parts as in all lives this an excellent classic that is not as well known as it should be. Originally published in 1928 but still readable today because human nature is still the same. the covered wagons have been replaced by auto</span>
  <span id="freeText1370472956665731023" style="display:none">This is a beautiful, poetic moving story of Abby Deal, covering the time of the early pioneer settlements in the Midwest.<br /><br />It is a timeless family story of a mother who sees the dreams she is unable to fulfill passed on to her children. Realistic--with both sad and funny parts as in all lives this an excellent classic that is not as well known as it should be. Originally published in 1928 but still readable today because human nature is still the same. the covered wagons have been replaced by autos and planes but a story of interesting people remains a good story. You won't regret reading this!!<br /><br />Highly recommended for any reader---but young girls with an interest in history will find it especially appealing.<br /><br />Read long ago before GR so dates unknown.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>
